  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a886859c-97da-4f64-a647-b8e6b49bd20c'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<div id="review_2298409556" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2298409556" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2298409556?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30604861-emma-giordano?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2298409556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15873775575751905907">Marissa Meyer has done it again. I am TRULY blown away by <i>Archenemies</i>. Stay tuned for my spoiler-filled video review!<br/><br/>CW: violence, oppression<br/><br/><i>Renegades</i> was already a fantastically constructed world, but <i>Archenemies</i> breaks the boundaries for what we know of Gatlon City. I cannot get enough of the politics of this world. Conflict goes far beyond what we already know of the Renegades’ power and the Anarchists’ will for vengeance. Morals are questioned, friends become suspects, and tensions are highe</span>
  <span id="freeText15873775575751905907" style="display:none">Marissa Meyer has done it again. I am TRULY blown away by <i>Archenemies</i>. Stay tuned for my spoiler-filled video review!<br /><br />CW: violence, oppression<br /><br /><i>Renegades</i> was already a fantastically constructed world, but <i>Archenemies</i> breaks the boundaries for what we know of Gatlon City. I cannot get enough of the politics of this world. Conflict goes far beyond what we already know of the Renegades’ power and the Anarchists’ will for vengeance. Morals are questioned, friends become suspects, and tensions are higher than ever. I really love the direction Marissa Meyer has taken with the second installment in terms of how superheroes are viewed and how supervillains are treated. The power dynamics in this story are captivating and complex, and I’m desperate for more.<br /><br />Once again, I love the cast of characters in this series. Every character, including many of the side characters, receive additional development that helps them to become authentic and refreshing. I loved watching Adrian and Nova grow as individuals and a team, alongside the rest of the Renegades and Anarchists. This series has one of the most compelling groups of companions I’ve read in YA in a very long time. Additionally, the romance is – once again – fabulous! I am <b>HERE</b> for more slow burn enemies-to-lovers (where-one-does-not-even-know-they-are-enemies) relationships. Nova and Adrian are a fierce, yet sweet couple, and I also loved the introduction of a new budding romance between teammates. Not only does this story have a wicked plot, but there’s a spectacular cast of characters holding it up.<br /><br />When comparing <i>Renegades</i> and <i>Archenemies</i>, I do feel I prefer <i>Renegades</i>, but only slightly. It’s even tough to say I ACTUALLY prefer one over the other because they are both remarkable in their own ways. As a plot-based reader, I prefer <i>Renegades</i> because it is more action-packed, but I do find myself also drawn to <i>Archenemies</i> for it’s strong and ever-developing political arc. Though that is my preference, I don’t think one is greatly “better” than the other. <i>Archenemies</i> is a satisfying sequel that will leave you wanting more and more.<br /><br /><i>Renegades</i> is amazing. <i>Archenemies</i> is equally amazing. I would highly highly recommend this series – it is one of my new absolute favorites of all time. One more note on the sequel though - Prepare yourselves for yet another unbearable ending . . .<br /><br /><i>I received a free copy of this book from Macmillan. I had no obligation to review this book and all opinions are my own.</i></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2397672908" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2397672908" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2397672908?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2397672908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13927505750923242347">I am trying so hard to love this series but it just isn't working.<br/><br/>After not enjoying <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36381037.Cinder__The_Lunar_Chronicles___1_' title='Cinder (The Lunar Chronicles, #1) by Marissa Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'> Cinder</a>, I went on to love the rest of the Lunar Chronicles, so I was really hoping I could do that with this series. I was hoping that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28421168.Renegades__Renegades___1_' title='Renegades (Renegades, #1) by Marissa Meyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Renegades</a> was just a shaky start to something much better. And, for a while, I convinced myself I liked this one more than the first. But aside from a few good bits, I think I'll just have to admit these books are not for me.<br/><br/>Let's break it down.<br/><br/><pre>
  <b>» The characters.</b>
</pre><br/>Honestly, I f</span>
  <span id="freeText13927505750923242347" style="display:none">I am trying so hard to love this series but it just isn't working.<br><br>After not enjoying <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36381037.Cinder__The_Lunar_Chronicles___1_" title="Cinder (The Lunar Chronicles, #1) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener"> Cinder</a>, I went on to love the rest of the Lunar Chronicles, so I was really hoping I could do that with this series. I was hoping that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28421168.Renegades__Renegades___1_" title="Renegades (Renegades, #1) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Renegades</a> was just a shaky start to something much better. And, for a while, I convinced myself I liked this one more than the first. But aside from a few good bits, I think I'll just have to admit these books are not for me.<br><br>Let's break it down.<br><br><pre>
  <b>» The characters.</b>
</pre><br>Honestly, I find almost everyone annoying and one-dimensional. Every single character is defined by their powers and has virtually no personality beyond this. Despite some attempts to add some morally grey areas, pretty much every character can be neatly separated into good guys or bad guys. It's so simplistic and bland. Plus, Adrian is sappy as all hell. Even Nova turns to mush in this book. Outside of those two, most of the characters feel interchangeable.<br><br><pre>
  <b>» The plot.</b>
</pre><br>What is the plot here? If it's supposed to be Nova's infiltration and revenge then, wow, that is not coming across very well. Maybe because she is just so bad at it. Is she even trying? It definitely doesn't feel like it. In fact, the whole "I hate the Renegades and must have revenge" angle seems like a poor cover for what is evidently <b>nothing but a romance.</b> And about that...<br><br><pre>
  <b>» The romance.</b>
</pre><br>In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28421168.Renegades__Renegades___1_" title="Renegades (Renegades, #1) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener"> Renegades</a>, romance sat quietly in the background, but here it is genuinely the whole book. This sequel became so unnecessarily cheesy and sappy. It felt like every single scene was an excuse for Nova to pretend to pretend to flirt with Adrian while actually just flirting with him. Afterwards, of course, she's all "shucks, why do I have these feelings? It's all part of the mission!"<br><br>And just... where’s the tension? There’s no way these two won’t end up together, right? No way. It’s so clear the way it’s headed that I find myself hoping I’ll be pleasantly surprised by Meyer having one of them fall off a building and die instead. Which, obviously, should not be my reaction to the central romance.<br><br>I also think I threw up in my mouth a little at the scene where Adrian <i>literally</i> makes Nova's dreams come true.<br><br><pre>
  <b>» The repetition.</b>
</pre><br>Seriously, I get it already! How many times will I have to read Nova's mantra about how the Renegades are just so terrible because they didn’t save her family? She has to think it again every few chapters, lest we stop being annoyed by it! In fact, every time she repeats something like:<br><blockquote>
  <i>This was why she was here. To put an end to the idolizing of these so-called heroes and the promises they made but couldn’t keep. The heroes who had not saved her family. Who had not saved her. The heroes who had ruined Ace.</i>
</blockquote><br>I find it less convincing. I think it's a weak idea anyway that she will betray these people she's become so close to because they weren't there to save her parents. Reiterating it doesn't make it any better.<br><br>I'm also tired of Nova insisting she is playing a part by flirting with Adrian then noting how she must “ignore” those strange feelings in her stomach. I gotta say, it didn’t feel much like “ignoring” because she brought it up in most of the chapters.<br><br><pre>
  <b>» Cheesy dialogue.</b>
</pre><br>To be fair, I think Meyer actually toned it down some in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35425827.Archenemies__Renegades___2_" title="Archenemies (Renegades, #2) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener"> Archenemies</a>. The superhero dialogue was even worse in the first book. Still, I cannot take it seriously when the characters say things like "Who are you?" "Your worst nightmare." It sounds so silly. That will ALWAYS make me think of...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1541808254ra/26571264.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I guess this particular brand of superhero story may not be for me. The tropes of the genre (such as how no one knows Adrian is The Sentinel even though he practically wears a sign saying "it is me") make it difficult for me to suspend disbelief, and the black and white view of good vs evil is uninteresting to me. I think it's all just very simplistic - from the characters' motivations to the standard YA romance. I also dislike the decision to have Adrian's tattoos be able to bestow any power or make someone immune to pretty much anything; it seems to defeat the point of everyone having unique powers and weaknesses.<br><br>Oh well, I gave it a good chance.<br><br><a href="http://emilymay.me" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13927505750923242347" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2548682078" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2548682078" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2548682078?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781250078308" href="/book/show/37508619-archenemies">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=auto-buy-authors">auto-buy-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=couldn-t-wait-to-read">couldn-t-wait-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=unpopular-opinion">unpopular-opinion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=from-publisher-author">from-publisher-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=diverse">diverse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2548682078" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8741628451741329204">happy book birthday to Archenemies!! my gift is that i posted this mildly negative full review on my blog. find it here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2018/11/06/disappointment-and-an-existential-crisis-renegades-and-archenemies-reviews/'>https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br/><br/>-----------<br/><br/>I’ve said it before and I’ll say it again: Life is teeming with disappointments.<br/><br/>The fact that that is closer than anything else to becoming my catchphrase is, in a word, concerning. I was hoping that when I inevitably developed a catchphrase, it’d be something cool, like “cleanup on aisle 7” (for when I commit murders) or “all</span>
  <span id="freeText8741628451741329204" style="display:none">happy book birthday to Archenemies!! my gift is that i posted this mildly negative full review on my blog. find it here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2018/11/06/disappointment-and-an-existential-crisis-renegades-and-archenemies-reviews/">https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br /><br />-----------<br /><br />I’ve said it before and I’ll say it again: Life is teeming with disappointments.<br /><br />The fact that that is closer than anything else to becoming my catchphrase is, in a word, concerning. I was hoping that when I inevitably developed a catchphrase, it’d be something cool, like “cleanup on aisle 7” (for when I commit murders) or “all in a day’s work” (for when I do something very cool that should not be a casual or daily occurrence).<br /><br />But this works too.<br /><br />Renegades was a meh read for me, but when I finished, I was like, “Potential!!” There were plotlines and relationships that were set up that I thought, if they played out a certain way, could be really fun. I had hopes for Archenemies.<br /><br />What I did not remember - which is crazy because I do pride myself on my pessimism - is that if things can go one way and go well, they can also go another way and go very badly. <br /><br />That is what happened here.<br /><br />Let’s go one by one.<br /><br /><b>THE CHARACTERS</b><br /><br />In my Renegades review, I basically listed off a bunch of characters and declared that I didn’t like any of them per se, but also didn’t dislike any of them, and if a very specific set of events occurred in Archenemies I could, perhaps, come away with an appreciation for one or two.<br /><br />Guess what didn’t happen.<br /><br />(The opposite happened.)<br /><br />The characters in this book were B A D. That’s right! No abstractions. They were straight up unpleasant, and/or non-present. Here was my ranking of ability-to-potentially-like-any-given-character, from “one cool fight scene and some banter” away to “this character would have to spend 500 pages being unadulteratedly amusing for me to even give half a sh*t, but theoretically anything’s possible.”<br /><br />- Nova<br />- Oscar<br />- Ruby<br />- Honey<br />- Adrian<br /><br />This is some high potential for me!! I almost never like characters. I’m picky. I have high standards. But I was <i>willing to believe.</i><br /><br />For you to fully understand the sheer extent to which my ability to hope was made a mockery, I need to tell you three simultaneous things that happened in this book.<br /><br />1. All characters except Nova (who I was closest to liking) and Adrian (least close) were basically dropped. We rarely heard from anyone except those two.<br /><br />2. Nova became insufferable.<br /><br />3. Adrian grew worse than I ever could have imagined.<br /><br />GUYS. IT WAS AWFUL. Honey and Ruby and Oscar, the only characters who were ever really even anywhere close to approaching funny? GONEZO. Sayonara! <br /><br />So now we are in the suffocating embrace of literally only Nova and Adrian (which is terrible for an additional reason that we will get to). Which would maybe be okay, if they were better than in Renegades, or even if they were exactly the same. I’m not asking for much.<br /><br />BUT APPARENTLY NOT MUCH IS TOO MUCH TO ASK FOR.<br /><br />Nova spends this entire book being overwhelmingly, unrelentingly selfish. She put the lives of children and innocents on the line, she manipulated perfectly nice people, she lied and stole and deceived, all to achieve her ends. And she was really annoying about it, too, which was the worst bit of all.<br /><br />Adrian was just Boring McBoringson. All he cared about was his dumb alter ego and his boring parents and guess what? I do not care about either of those things.<br /><br />It’s such a long character development arc, from all-evil/all-good to complex, and the second book really gets the short end of the stick for that. Basically both Adrian and Nova spent the whole time in one (1) repetitive thought process, which wasn’t even interesting in the first place.<br /><br />Except for one other thought process.<br /><br /><br /><b>THE ROMANCE</b><br /><br />Picture me dramatically collapsing to my knees, shaking my fists beseechingly at the sky, screaming “NOOOOO!”<br /><br />For, my friends, I have been made a fool of.<br /><br />I never like romances. I especially never like them in YA fantasy. They always feel extraneous and dull and unremarkable. But for Renegades...I put it all on the line.<br /><br />The romance between Nova and Adrian in Renegade was veryyy slow, and awkward, and cute. It was a side-plot and it didn’t overtake any of the more interesting stuff. I thought it was exactly what a romance in YA fantasy should look like, if there has to be one at all.<br /><br />But, as mentioned, Marissa Meyer took my risking of it all and PUT IT THROUGH A PAPER SHREDDER. AND THEN PICKED UP THE PIECES AND LAUGHED AND THEN EVERYONE ELSE LAUGHED. (That’s where the being made a fool of comes in.)<br /><br />The romance in this book was suffocating and overwhelming and insta-love-y and sentimental and cheesy and everywhere and INESCAPABLE.<br /><br />I hated it so much. And the fact that I had already come to hate both the characters involved just made me hate it <i>even more</i>. <br /><br />Forming a hatred so powerful it probably qualifies as one of the C-minus level superpowers in this book.<br /><br /><br /><b>THE PLOT</b><br /><br />The last book set up a very cool and complex moral exploration - essentially what Wildcard wishes and prays it could do - but it got old fast in this book. It was way too hit-you-over-the-head. If it remained a background theme, that would have been great, but instead every conversation and internal monologue had to brush up against it.<br /><br />And by brush up against it, I mean “hit it with the force of one of those really jump scare-y don’t-drive-distracted commercials where a bunch of friends are in a car texting and then the car gets hit by like the biggest 18-wheeler you have seen in your life.”<br /><br />Very subtle. Blink and you’ll miss it type of stuff.<br /><br />Overall, the plotline of this was better than the last one (which had the weirdest full book + one half of another book structure of all time), but it still mostly came into play in the ending.<br /><br />The ending, however, was fantastic. And I think it also sets up what could be a really interesting plotline for the next book. It has potential.<br /><br />But we’ve all learned how that goes.<br /><br />Bottom line: I think I’ll stick with this series, but that also might just be because of how dearly I love to suffer.<br /><br />------<br /><i>tbr review</i><br /><br />out here getting BLESSED with ARCs of highly anticipated sequels when i haven't even started the series yet!!<br /><br />&amp; oh boy this is long.<br /><br />also renegades is long.<br /><br />...<br /><br />i have a lot of reading to do.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8741628451741329204" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12418668428047183866">i feel like i could copy and paste my review for <i>‘renegades’</i> and everything would apply to this sequel. we stan a consistent series! lol. <br/><br/>again, this series is the only story i have read where the plot centres around crime fighting superheroes. like actual heroes vs. villains. and i forget how cheesy it can be at times, especially during the action sequences. literally all that is missing is a POW or BAM in little balloon bubbles down the margins. but once you get past that, the story is actuall</span>
  <span id="freeText12418668428047183866" style="display:none">i feel like i could copy and paste my review for <i>‘renegades’</i> and everything would apply to this sequel. we stan a consistent series! lol. <br /><br />again, this series is the only story i have read where the plot centres around crime fighting superheroes. like actual heroes vs. villains. and i forget how cheesy it can be at times, especially during the action sequences. literally all that is missing is a POW or BAM in little balloon bubbles down the margins. but once you get past that, the story is actually quite decent. slow, but decent. <br /><br />i will admit, i think series would have benefited from being a duology. it often feels like theres not enough content to stretch across three books. and because of that, there is a lot of filler and slow moments to trudge through. but, similar to <i>‘renegades,’</i> everything picks up towards the end. and when it picks up, i mean like 100mph fast. like, holy cow. the lines have become so blurred, its not even funny.   <br /><br />and once more, the book ends on a cliff hanger. the cliff hanger from the first book is not really a focal point in the sequel, which i thought it would be. so it will be interesting to see how this one is addressed in the final book!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_2788506001" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2788506001" />
    <a title="Angelica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16201093-angelica"><img alt="Angelica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507050077p2/16201093.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2788506001?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angelica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angelica" href="/user/show/16201093-angelica">Angelica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=super-powers">super-powers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=three-star">three-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=release-2018">release-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=authors-i-love">authors-i-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2788506001" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17089481017617343458"><b>This book was so long!!!!! And absolutely no reason!<br/><br/>Don't get me wrong, I was entertained. At times I didn't even notice the time passing. Other times it felt like it was never going to end!</b><br/><br/>I keep wanting to love this series. I keep wanting to love these characters the same way I loved the characters of Meyer's Lunar Chronicles. I tried, guys, I really did. And I just couldn't.<br/><br/><b>My first issue was the charcters.</b><br/><br/>Aside from Adrian and Nova, none of these characters mattered. They were two dimensiona</span>
  <span id="freeText17089481017617343458" style="display:none"><b>This book was so long!!!!! And absolutely no reason!<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, I was entertained. At times I didn't even notice the time passing. Other times it felt like it was never going to end!</b><br /><br />I keep wanting to love this series. I keep wanting to love these characters the same way I loved the characters of Meyer's Lunar Chronicles. I tried, guys, I really did. And I just couldn't.<br /><br /><b>My first issue was the charcters.</b><br /><br />Aside from Adrian and Nova, none of these characters mattered. They were two dimensional and honestly, pretty interchangeable. The story would have gone the same without them. If anything, it might have made the book shorter which I honestly wouldn't have minded.<br /><br />And even Adrian and Nova were pretty bland. Adrian was my favorite in this book, which isn't really saying much, all things considered. And I have to admit, I only really liked him because his powers were pretty cool and he could easily be the worlds greatest superhero... or villain if he wanted.<br /><br />Nova, on the other hand, was kind of annoying. Her hate towards the Renegades always seemed like a weak plot point. Yes, she should be wary about all the laws the Renegades make, but having this personal vendetta because they didn't save her all those years ago just seems childish.  They were probably busy doing other hero stuff. They aren't omniscient, it's not like they knew she was in trouble!<br /><br /><b>Then there was the plot... or lack thereof.</b><br /><br />You'd think that a book that was almost 600 pages would have a plot, right? Well, no, you'd be terribly wrong.<br /><br />It's supposed to be a revenge plot with villains and heroes. It's supposed to be a battle of superpowers and skill. We barely get to actually see any of that though.<br /><br />Nova spends the entire time going through a repetitive mantra of how the Renegades are horrible and should be removed from power, and then going on in a ramble about how maybe, just maybe the Renegades weren't all bad.<br /><br />Also, the dialogue is pure cheese. It was funny and cringy all at once. I don't know if I hated it or if I secretly loved it. I think I secretly loved it, not gonna lie.<br /><br /><b>All of that said, I was pretty entertained. Also, I now have several theories of where this story is going to go and I'm looking forward to reading the third book and see where it goes.</b><br /><br />So, do I recommend it? Maybe?<br /><br />I have no idea. Read at your own risk.<br /><br /><br />Follow Me Here Too:<b> <a href="http://www.thebookcovergirls.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/covergirlreads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/book-cover-girl-19339391" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin'</a> || <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookcovergirls//" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://thebookcovergirls.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/thebookcovergirls/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17089481017617343458" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2398254461" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2398254461" />
    <a title="Hamad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad"><img alt="Hamad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577880699p2/54464244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2398254461?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hamad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hamad" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad">Hamad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=good-covers">good-covers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2398254461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3845656322384690925"> This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2018/11/21/archenemies-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>@The Book Prescription</a><br/><br/> <i>“I just want to remind you that there are no lone wolves in the Renegades. There is no I in hero.”</i><br/><br/>🌟 I insist on calling Marissa Meyer the queen of re-tellings. TLC is one of my favorite series that kept improving somehow till the last book. I expected Marissa to be awesome when she writes an original series, except that it was not original!<br/><br/>🌟Jump back a few years ago to when the X-Men movies were released, particularl</span>
  <span id="freeText3845656322384690925" style="display:none"> This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2018/11/21/archenemies-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">@The Book Prescription</a><br /><br /> <i>“I just want to remind you that there are no lone wolves in the Renegades. There is no I in hero.”</i><br /><br />🌟 I insist on calling Marissa Meyer the queen of re-tellings. TLC is one of my favorite series that kept improving somehow till the last book. I expected Marissa to be awesome when she writes an original series, except that it was not original!<br /><br />🌟Jump back a few years ago to when the X-Men movies were released, particularly the 3rd movie. Which I watched a million times on a DVD player back in the day where there were not many options to choose from. The point is that this book felt like a YA retelling of that movie rather than being an original.<br /><br />🌟 I don’t have any problems with Marissa’s writing style and I probably shouldn’t after 8 books. Although some of the conversations felt comical more than realistic but that didn’t bother me.<br /><br />🌟 The other problem I had was the slow pacing, for the first 50-60% of the book, pretty much nothing important happened and it was repetitive. The book is a large one that could have been cut to half and still delivered the same story.<br /><br />🌟 I like the characters. And though I was rooting for The Anarchists rather than The Renegades, this book focused on the later group which made me feel something was missing.🌟 As I was saying above the plot was easy to predict. Specially if you are into superheroes and super powers. I can’t stop thinking of some characters as characters in the X-Men movie which is sad.<br /><br />🌟 Summary: I originally read this because it was supposed to be a duology and it is now a trilogy. Something that made me skeptical and it looks my fears were in the right place. It should have been faster, shorter and more original. I am still invested enough to read the last book and I hope it doesn’t become longer than that. I ended up being generous and gave it 3 out of 5 stars.<br /><br />🌟 Prescription: If you like superheroes but hasn’t watched/ read books like that then this may be for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3845656322384690925" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I'm also a little disappointed in both of them for not figuring it out though. Neither of them seem particularly subtle, but especially Nova. She is so outspoken about Agent N and Ace Anarchy's helmet that someone other than the now trapped Danna really should have caught on by now.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />But I might just die of impatience because I neeeeeeeeed the third book NOW PLEAAAASSSEEEEEEEEEEE!!!!</span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781250078308" href="/book/show/37508619-archenemies">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2186330834" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10106015447103634936"><b>2.5</b><br/><br/>I still think Meyer is one of the best fantasy YA author out there, and I still think she doesn't even have to try to be able to stand out. But <b>this book just didn't work</b>. Personally, I believe that the reason (at least in my case) is one of <b>disappointed expectations</b>: like many other fans, I had got used to the idea that the Renegades series was going to be a duology, and only recently did I find out that this was not the case any longer. Not only that, but<b> <i>Archenemies</i></b>, the second book I, and</span>
  <span id="freeText10106015447103634936" style="display:none"><b>2.5</b><br /><br />I still think Meyer is one of the best fantasy YA author out there, and I still think she doesn't even have to try to be able to stand out. But <b>this book just didn't work</b>. Personally, I believe that the reason (at least in my case) is one of <b>disappointed expectations</b>: like many other fans, I had got used to the idea that the Renegades series was going to be a duology, and only recently did I find out that this was not the case any longer. Not only that, but<b> <i>Archenemies</i></b>, the second book I, and we all, longed for for so long, on top of <i>not</i> being the finale we wanted, <b>also feels rather static</b>: it is probably unfair to say that this book is devoid of any major turning point in the wider picture of the series's plot; one or two important things do happen, after all, but compared to the length of the novel itself, it is not sufficient at all. It fell dramatically flat. It's not that it was <i>bad</i>; but it <i>was</i> <b>disastrously unfulfilling</b>. <br /><br />Nevertheless, I would like to point out that the series still poses <b>a range of moral issues</b> which I believe <b>will prove very interesting for the younger audience</b> that it targets. I say specifically 'younger audience' because, while the book's themes may certainly interest a wider public, the treatment of said themes is still not complex enough as to make them stimulating for somewhat more mature readers. So if you are looking for a book to give to your kids, choose <i>Renegades</i>—or Marissa Meyer in general. I promise they'll thank you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10106015447103634936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4801798066937152267"> I don't love this book as much as the first one. I got bored with Nova's third job at Renegades HQ. That portion is excruciatingly lengthy to get through. Callum tried hard to keep the artifacts upbeat but it's like browsing through a museum. I enjoyed the start of the book before Nova started her third job. I enjoyed the ending as well. The villains' win at their mission and lost of their *** is a surprise one for me. Normally I don't like Villains but I'm liking Nightmare and the banters amon</span>
  <span id="freeText4801798066937152267" style="display:none"> I don't love this book as much as the first one. I got bored with Nova's third job at Renegades HQ. That portion is excruciatingly lengthy to get through. Callum tried hard to keep the artifacts upbeat but it's like browsing through a museum. I enjoyed the start of the book before Nova started her third job. I enjoyed the ending as well. The villains' win at their mission and lost of their *** is a surprise one for me. Normally I don't like Villains but I'm liking Nightmare and the banters among her group.<br /><br /> This book is told in the third person point of view following Adrian, Renegade team leader and son of Renegade original founders, as he and his teammates attempted to apprehend a band of thieves leaving the hospital with their stolen bags of pills. Adrian is still in search of his mother's killer and he doesn't believe Nightmare is dead. The alternating view is Nova, a villain called Nightmare is spying on the Renegades by becoming a Renegade herself, a position she won through trial competition. This book continues from book one where the recent villain, the Detonator harm a lot of innocent civilians and the Renegades are introducing a weapon that will take away the supper powers of prodigy lawbreakers. From the surprise ending of book 1, Nova's new mission is more important now than ever and she can't fail.<br /><br /> Archenemies is filled with thoughts of wanting the world rid of superheroes. Readers get to follow the lives of the heroes and villains in normal day to day life. It seems not much difference because there are bullies among the heroes and they act like any villains. The romance escalated another step in this sequel and Adrian is so cute when he's nervous. Some superpowers are pretty cool like Monarch and Adrian's drawing. I like Ruby and Oscar's attempts at love or Ruby's attempts at playing hard to get. Out of the first two books, I enjoyed the first one more. I can't wait to read Supernova, the finale to the series.<br /><br />xoxo, <br />Jasmine at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.howusefulitis.wordpress.com">www.howusefulitis.wordpress.com</a> for more details </span>

Am. Done. </u></i></b>   <br /><br />Thank you, Marissa Meyer, for signing my death certificate. Maybe I’ll come back as Phobia and be your worst fear. Though, even that wouldn’t be enough in my eyes after that heart breaking ending you delivered to us. <br /><br />Do I seriously have to wait a year for the third and final book? I think I just died a little more with that thought. <br /><br />I’m ending this without my heart and soul in tact. From now on, I’m going to be known as soulless Cassie. That’s it, that’s all I got for you. Goodbye. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7481532703985958529" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2301378673" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2301378673" />
    <a title="Kelly Brigid ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24407332-kelly-brigid"><img alt="Kelly Brigid ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557200443p2/24407332.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2301378673?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly Brigid ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly Brigid ♡" href="/user/show/24407332-kelly-brigid">Kelly Brigid ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24407332-kelly-brigid?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24407332-kelly-brigid?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24407332-kelly-brigid?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24407332-kelly-brigid?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24407332-kelly-brigid?shelf=superheroes">superheroes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2301378673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7103998364003129428"><i>
  <blockquote>“There were still consequences. There were always consequences, no matter which side she was on.”</blockquote>
</i><br/>♡ <b>I’m utterly torn.</b> I love the sweet characters and prodigy society depicted in general. But, I can’t overlook the glaring <b>similarities between this novel and the third installment in the X-men franchise, <i>The Last Stand.</i></b> One of the central plot points involves a drug that can neutralize the abilities of any prodigy. Nova is concerned that this power will be abused in the hands of egotistical Rene</span>
  <span id="freeText7103998364003129428" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>“There were still consequences. There were always consequences, no matter which side she was on.”</blockquote>
</i><br />♡ <b>I’m utterly torn.</b> I love the sweet characters and prodigy society depicted in general. But, I can’t overlook the glaring <b>similarities between this novel and the third installment in the X-men franchise, <i>The Last Stand.</i></b> One of the central plot points involves a drug that can neutralize the abilities of any prodigy. Nova is concerned that this power will be abused in the hands of egotistical Renegades, and thereby attempts to find a way to prevent its usage. Baring such a remarkable resemblance to the plot in the X-men movie, truly dampened my overall enjoyment.<br /><br />♡ <b>The pacing is painfully slow during the first half of the novel.</b> I honestly don’t mind it much when a story is slow-paced. I often welcome it! After all, <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> is one of my favorite novels ever written, and it’s a whopping 1,100 pages. There does however, need to be enough developments presented to hold my interest. I found this unfortunately, was lacking in Archenemies. Every turn of event felt either drawn out, repetitive, or unnecessary. Perhaps this is a side effect from a duology becoming a trilogy, but I would’ve greatly preferred it if the story was several hundred pages shorter.<br /><br />♡ <b>The romance in all its slow-burning beauty … withered and died?</b> How Nova and Adrien’s relationship develops in this book is disappointing to say the least. Their interactions were cute at times, but for the most part, too time-consuming and unnecessarily convoluted. It could’ve been simple and straightforward, but Nova incessantly stresses over her feelings for him, weaving together a (550 page-long) web of teenage angst and confusion. She has several agendas occurring at once that encourage this relationship to reach new depths, yet her guilt-laden conscience constantly causes her to hesitate. It’s highly frustrating and grows wearisome after a while.<br /><br />♡ <b>Bring on the moral dilemmas!</b> I mentioned this in my review for <i>Renegades</i> as well, but the morally grey areas depicted in this society are wonderful! Mostly evident through Nova’s character, the fine line between what makes someone a hero or villain is fascinating. Not unlike most situations in our lives, it’s challenging to devise a solution that will satisfy everyone. The numerous perspectives on the humane use of Agent N, Renegade laws, treatment of Anarchists, etc. is such a treat to read about!<br /><br />♡ <b>Out with a bang!</b> Despite its lethargic start, the last 100 pages of the novel is spectacular! It’s fast paced and riveting, with just enough emotional anxiety and agony to keep you on your toes. As a matter of fact, the conclusion felt so cohesive and entertaining that I find it startling to believe that it’s part of the same novel. The action sequences felt comical (as expected of a superhero novel) throughout most of the story but dives down a darker path in the finale. Foreshadowing a grittier sequel, perhaps?<br /><br />♡ <b>Archenemies certainly has a few faults, but it delivers where it matters.</b> The story is entertaining, the side characters are endearing when they make appearances, and the socio-political factors discussed throughout are highly intriguing! I’ll be holding onto the hope that the last book, <i>Supernova</i>, seals the deal! Wishing for better pacing, more side character love (where have my babies flown off to? I need them!), and less romantic angst! Marissa Meyer, I believe in you!<br /><br /><i>I received an ARC from the publisher in exchange for an honest review. Thank you!</i><br /><br /><a href="https://justanotherbookinthewall.wordpress.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/anotherbookinthewall/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/kelly_reads" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/anotherbookinthewall/pins/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/another-book-in-wall-18441447" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7103998364003129428" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2019">2019</a>,

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17341259177455129823">I am enjoying this series a lot so far. The writing is reminding me a lot of The Lunar Chronicles, which I enjoyed quite a lot, so I am quite pleased. Meyers characters are always interesting and fun to get to know. Also I love how unique this series continues to be with a different take on the superhero genre.<br/><br/>My only complaint about this book is there was quite a large chunk in the middle where things got a bit slow and stagnant. Meyer picked one major plot point and then just ran it into the g</span>
  <span id="freeText17341259177455129823" style="display:none">I am enjoying this series a lot so far. The writing is reminding me a lot of The Lunar Chronicles, which I enjoyed quite a lot, so I am quite pleased. Meyers characters are always interesting and fun to get to know. Also I love how unique this series continues to be with a different take on the superhero genre.<br /><br />My only complaint about this book is there was quite a large chunk in the middle where things got a bit slow and stagnant. Meyer picked one major plot point and then just ran it into the ground. I am attempting to avoid spoilers so I can't get into exactly what it was too much, but I will say it involved personal relationships and long conversations and after a while I was ready to move on. In a small dose I was fine with it, but it just got to be too much for me.<br /><br />My favorite part of this series is how it looks into the good that is inherent in villany and the bad that is inherent in heroics. It isn't just the good guys are good and the bad guys are bad and that is kind of awesome. I look forward to finding out where this goes with the next book as it is not quite clear yet who I will end up cheering for.<br /><br />If you like superheroes and don't mind a little YA romance mixed in, give this a shot. If you liked Cinder, I think you will enjoy this because it is written in the same vein.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17341259177455129823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2628639105" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2628639105" />
    <a title="ℨαrα " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57602032-r"><img alt="ℨαrα " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577832613p2/57602032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ℨαrα " class="user" itemprop="url" name="ℨαrα " href="/user/show/57602032-r">ℨαrα </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57602032-r?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer7242714985325666520"> <i>please note that the use of the terms “Nova’s mission” and reference to Nova being a “spy” are used VERY loosely in this review. </i> <br/><br/><b>
  <u>Things I liked:</u>
</b> <br/>◘ So like with renegades, <u>the ending</u> was REALLY GOOD. I genuinely enjoyed it. The Sentinel’s discovery and the party and the chaos at the very very end. WAS <i>GOOD.</i> <br/>◘ And at the risk of repeating my words in my Renegades review, Book 3 has potential and some really interesting things were set up at the end.<br/>◘ The very morally grey Renegades-Anarchist</span>
  <span id="freeText7242714985325666520" style="display:none"> <i>please note that the use of the terms “Nova’s mission” and reference to Nova being a “spy” are used VERY loosely in this review. </i> <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Things I liked:</u>
</b> <br />◘ So like with renegades, <u>the ending</u> was REALLY GOOD. I genuinely enjoyed it. The Sentinel’s discovery and the party and the chaos at the very very end. WAS <i>GOOD.</i> <br />◘ And at the risk of repeating my words in my Renegades review, Book 3 has potential and some really interesting things were set up at the end.<br />◘ The very morally grey Renegades-Anarchists-prodigy situation is good <s>but that was kinda ruined by Agent N. cough. I’ll elaborate later in the review.</s><br />◘ I LIKED DANNA. A LOT. Why? Because she’s nice, kind, friendly, a good prodigy, etc, etc. But she’s also <u>not blind to what’s right in front of her. </u>She’s the only one with an ounce of sense.<s>too bad she wasn’t in the book much. Nor were Ruby or Oscar or Honey.</s><br />◘ I'm curious about Phobia's identity and backstory.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Things I disliked:</u>
</b> <br />◘ So in a nutshell, I was so bored and couldn’t take anything seriously.<br />◘ “But Zara,” you say, “there was more action throughout the book when compared with Renegades. Why ever were you bored?” Well, I’ll tell you why. THE ROMANCE WAS STIFLING EVERYTHING. <br />◘ So was Nova. I liked her in book 1. Genuinely. In THIS BOOK, oh boy did she make my blood pressure skyrocket every time she was in any scene. which was for 95% of the book.<br />◘ In Renegades, the romance was a subplot, slow burn, on the back burner type of thing. I found it sweet and endearing and really didn’t mind it. But in this one, it was front and centre and it just went downhill. In my opinion. <br />◘ So Nova is flirting with Adrian to use it to her own benefit because she’s…*whispers so that the renegades don’t hear* she’s a <i>spy</i>. Just kidding, they won’t suspect a thing, you know, because Nova is an angle with whom they’ll trust their lives despite her sketchy behaviour because whatever she says is gospel. A true angel she is.<br />◘ ANYWAYS, Nova is flirting with Adrian and here’s her thought processes that are repeated every 5 pages (as much as I wish it was, this is not even an exaggeration): <br />“<i>I must destroy the Renegades who didn’t come when I needed them the most. But they aren’t ALL bad. What do I do?? I must flirt with Adrian to aid me in destroying the Renegades. But why am I feeling these feelings for him?? This is only for the purpose of the mission. Is what we have not real? Why isn’t Adrian interested in me anymore when I made it clear that I wasn’t interested in the previous book?? This hurts. bUt what we have isn’t real ,and I must destroy the Renegades.</i> etc, etc. In. every. scene. Need I say more?<br />◘ As for why I could not take this book seriously, its because NOBODY (excluding the aforementioned Danna) saw past Nova’s “ruse”. They ignored the most obvious signs. Nova might as well have been standing with a bright neon yellow sign that said “I WORK WITH THE ANARCHISTS” in bold, all caps lettering, but they STILL ate up every lie she spoon-fed them. It was wholly, utterly ridiculous. <br />◘ This also meant that clever deceit, subtle strategising and planning, true betrayal and moral conflict — elements that would’ve been true strengths and assets — felt so surface-level and artificial. It doesn’t feel to me like there were stakes. IM NOT BUYING IT AND I DONT CARE. <br />◘ And last but not least, our wonderful Agent N is an element I didn't really like. here's why: <br />1. Renegades has <b>Agent X</b>. <i>X-Men: The Last Stand</i> has the <b>Mutant Cure</b>.<br />2. Leech, from X-Men <i>neutralises</i> the powers of mutants who are near him, and was confined within Alcatraz. Max from Renegades <i>absorbs</i> the powers of prodigies who are near him and was quarantined within Renegades headquarters. <br />3. Leech happens to play a pivotal role in creating the Mutant cure. Max also may or may not play a pivotal role in creating Agent X. <br />I’m just baffled that <i>nobody</i> involved in the publishing process picked up on these similarities. <br /><br />A LOT of people actually enjoyed Archenemies more than they enjoyed Renegades, so take this review with a grain of salt <s>even though I was very, very salty</s>. But I'm not going to lie, my inner Slytherin didn’t mind terribly ripping this book to shreds. Yes I'm awful, I know this. <br /><br /><b>Overall rating:</b> ★★☆☆☆</span>
  <a data-text-id="7242714985325666520" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

And I love hanging with so many different types of powers. <br/>-slooooowww burn romance. I just like the way Marissa Meyer writes romances. It just connects with me for some reason, and I dig these two together (even though I dont fully dig them on their own)<br/><br/>What I didn't like:<br/>-nova. I didn't dis</span>
  <span id="freeText12322226796458651447" style="display:none">3.5 -&gt; rounding up to a 4<br /><br />What I liked:<br />- the setting. This is just a fun place to hang out. This world where people with superpowers are the only really relevant people and everyone (almost) is morally gray. And I love hanging with so many different types of powers. <br />-slooooowww burn romance. I just like the way Marissa Meyer writes romances. It just connects with me for some reason, and I dig these two together (even though I dont fully dig them on their own)<br /><br />What I didn't like:<br />-nova. I didn't dislike her in the first book, I was nurtal. In this one she got on my nerves. The thing is, she's not good at accomplishing her goals. We go through long stretches of time where she just does nothing to help her fellow bad guys take the good guys down, and in the meantime, we get about sixteen rants about why she needs to take them down and how much she hates them. She starts to come off like an all talk villian. Which is annoying because she actually is capable, but she just doesn't DO ANYTHING so she just talks about all she COULD do. <br />- filler. It's a filler book. Nothing happened in this whole book until the end. A new ellement is added and the entire book consists of talking and speculating about how this new ellement could possibly maybe probably effect the world. And we progress the romance. That's it. Thats 400 pages. Speculation and kissy faces. Until the ending which was cool (but a bit predictable). <br /><br />Here's the thing, even though my two negatives are big negatives, I just really enjoyed reading it. I guess this author just connects with me because she constantly does stuff I don't like, yet I almost always come out of her books smiling. This was a book where very little happened (until the end) but I had a really good time hanging out here. <br /><br />I don't think this needed to be expanded to three books, but I'm looking forward to the third one anyway 😄</span>

<div id="review_2313229884" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2313229884" />
    <a title="Kay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76080680-kay"><img alt="Kay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551488292p2/76080680.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2313229884?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kay" href="/user/show/76080680-kay">Kay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76080680-kay?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76080680-kay?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2313229884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12502308732271202684">It's finally happened. After a whole year of anticipation, I FINALLY read my most anticipated most awaited most I MUST READ THIS AIOSKLJFDAIOFSJ book of 2019 and I have fEELINGS. Note: there will be spoilers for Renegades (the first book in the trilogy) but not Archenemies in this review.<br/><br/>Archenemies picks up a little after the first book left off, after the explosive battle that killed The Detonator and shocking revelation that Ace Anarchy is, in fact, still alive. It's been a year since I read </span>
  <span id="freeText12502308732271202684" style="display:none">It's finally happened. After a whole year of anticipation, I FINALLY read my most anticipated most awaited most I MUST READ THIS AIOSKLJFDAIOFSJ book of 2019 and I have fEELINGS. Note: there will be spoilers for Renegades (the first book in the trilogy) but not Archenemies in this review.<br /><br />Archenemies picks up a little after the first book left off, after the explosive battle that killed The Detonator and shocking revelation that Ace Anarchy is, in fact, still alive. It's been a year since I read the first one, but I was able to quickly recall what happened within the first couple of chapters and it was so exciting to be able to dive back into this phenomenal world!<br /><br />Like the first book, this one still centers around the struggle between "good" and "bad," whether there really is a good or bad, if it's so black and white, or if we're all a bit grey. There's the introduction of new "Agent N" that was teased in the last book, and it really added to Nova's struggle, I feel! She also gets to know more of the Renegades, know them better, and has to consider where her true alliances really lie, and I loved seeing that struggle really develop! In addition, we now have scenes with the feared Ace Anarchy, who is still firmly on the sides of the Anarchists, and is still Nova's wonderful uncle, juxtaposed against the Renegades she spends so much time with!<br /><br />This book did feel a bit slow at times in terms of the action, instead devoting more time to character development, which I both liked and disliked. For a superhero novel, I would have liked a bit more action and things to happen, but at the same time character development is so important! <br /><br />The character development really gave more time to the budding relationship between Nova and Adrian! These two are so cute, and of course I'm such a sucker for slow burn relationships! There are some sweet awkward scenes too that are fun to read about, just screaming for them to get together already!<br /><br />Unfortunately, I felt that this sweet character development between Nova and Adrian was at the expense of the other characters. I still love Oscar! He's so funny and also his love for food is basically me in a nutshell get someone who likes you as much as Oscar loves food haha. I would have really liked to see more of the other Anarchists though: Leroy and Honey and Phobia, who seemed to be much more prevalent in the first book than this one.<br /><br />The one thing that really kind of bugged me about this book was that there were a couple of things that happened in the last book that I was hoping would be explained more here. For example, how is it that Nova survives and kills Ingrid when it seemed so inevitable that Nightmare had died in the first book? Also, why did we pretend that Ace Anarchy was dead for the entire first book, when he seems normal here besides to have a big reveal? I was hoping a few questions would be answered, and they weren't and that sort of makes it feel like a plot hole? But this isn't the last book so I still have hope and if they're answered in the third book all will be forgiven haha. <br /><br />While I would have enjoyed a bit more action, the action scenes that we did have certainly did not disappoint! The book opens with an awesome sequence against a new villain that I loved, and the conclusion is even more incredible! I was on pins and needles the whole time the ending was happening, and it was everything I could have hoped for and omgomgomg I need the next book so much!!!!<br /><br />Overall, I didn't enjoy this book quite as much as I was hoping, and not quite as much as I enjoyed Renegades or any of Meyer's other books, but I still really liked it and would definitely recommend you read it! (Although now I'm suffering because I spent the entire year anticipating it and devoured it in one afternoon and now I have to wait another year again...) Now, we only have to wait and see if it's more of a Lunar Chronicles ending or a Heartless one...I'm hoping for something in the middle haha!<br /><br />4 stars<br />---<br /><br />Since this book comes out in less than two weeks and will inevitably be reviewed by lots of amazing popular reviewers (whose reviews I can't wait to read!) and I will be pushed down, I'd like to take a moment to appreciate how I was once the 8th most liked review lolll. <br /><br />also ALSDKFJAOIESKLJF OAWIEKJFSD OWJIOELKDSJF OWIJSDKF IT COMES OUT IN LESS THAN TWO WEEKS<br /><br />-----<br />5/18/18<br />THE COVER IS ART<br /><br />AND ITS A TRILOGY OMGOMGOMGOMG</span>
  <a data-text-id="12502308732271202684" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2313229884">

<div id="review_2420228704" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2420228704" />
    <a title="Althea | themoonwholistens ☾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59033840-althea-themoonwholistens"><img alt="Althea | themoonwholistens ☾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597139554p2/59033840.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2420228704?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Althea | themoonwholistens ☾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Althea | themoonwholistens ☾" href="/user/show/59033840-althea-themoonwholistens">Althea | themoonwholistens ☾</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781250078308" href="/book/show/37508619-archenemies">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59033840-althea-themoonwholistens?shelf=best-audiobooks">best-audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59033840-althea-themoonwholistens?shelf=read-audiobook">read-audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59033840-althea-themoonwholistens?shelf=rep-poc">rep-poc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59033840-althea-themoonwholistens?shelf=genre-dystopia-scifi">genre-dystopia-scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59033840-althea-themoonwholistens?shelf=made-me-cry-and-my-heart-ache">made-me-cry-and-my-heart-ache</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59033840-althea-themoonwholistens?shelf=age-young-adult">age-young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2420228704" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17922586391885610802"><i>“To know what this world could look like, what humanity could be, if only we all chose to do our best, to help others, to...to be, well, heroes.” </i><br/><br/><b>FORMAT READ:</b> Audiobook<br/><b>SIMILAR VIBES:</b> The Young Elites, The Darkest Minds<br/><br/>⟹ <a href='https://themoonwholistens.wixsite.com/mysite' rel='nofollow noopener'>MY BLOG</a> ⟸<br/>⟹ <a>SUPPORT ME ON KO-FI</a> ⟸<br/><i>*All of my reviews are as spoiler-free as possible unless states otherwise* </i><br/><br/><b>
  <u>OVERALL:</u>
</b> 3.5<br/>Compared to the first book… I liked this one more in terms of plot and themes. I feel like there was more happening in the plot and world-building was able </span>
  <span id="freeText17922586391885610802" style="display:none"><i>“To know what this world could look like, what humanity could be, if only we all chose to do our best, to help others, to...to be, well, heroes.” </i><br /><br /><b>FORMAT READ:</b> Audiobook<br /><b>SIMILAR VIBES:</b> The Young Elites, The Darkest Minds<br /><br />⟹ <a href="https://themoonwholistens.wixsite.com/mysite" rel="nofollow noopener">MY BLOG</a> ⟸<br />⟹ <a>SUPPORT ME ON KO-FI</a> ⟸<br /><i>*All of my reviews are as spoiler-free as possible unless states otherwise* </i><br /><br /><b>
  <u>OVERALL:</u>
</b> 3.5<br />Compared to the first book… I liked this one more in terms of plot and themes. I feel like there was more happening in the plot and world-building was able to expand more in this book. It was more thought-provoking, in my opinion, and I really thought that the themes that the series is trying to communicate were much more prominent. It hit me in the face a lot more.<br /><br />That guy that Nova works with is my favourite character in the whole book even though I cannot remember his name. And the Nova-Adrian relationship interests me more than their individuals characters though… which is... I don't know how to feel about that yet BUT I LIKE THEM<br /><br />The other character relationships ARE MY ABSOLUTE FAVOURITE as well !!! I probably can't say exactly which ones because erm spoilers... I have a lot of problems with the characters themselves but I like how they interact and the dynamic between the characters are something that I really enjoyed and was what ultimately kept me going. I absolutely adored the family representations in this book. They aren’t very explicitly described and focused on but that is part of why I liked it. It's one of the underlying themes and is part of the emotional gut punches every now and then.<br /><br />A lot of lines made me cringe, however, and I couldn't help but pause to catch myself. But I do like the way battle scenes are written. It was descriptive enough for a fantasy novel without it being too flowery which is sometimes what puts me off in certain books.<br /><br />It was a lot less focused on neither the Renegades or the Archanists which kind of disappointed me. Though, it gave room for more of Nova-Adrian time. And even then, there was just enough emotional punch that made me want to keep reading and reading and reading !!<br /><br />I think that the pacing of these books is the problem as I like fast-paced books and I just never feel like a lot of things happened. You can combine the plots of the first and second book into one and all will be good and fine. Although, I do understand that it makes this book more suitable for those slow-paces fantasy readers that enjoy the suspense behind Nova and Adrian's secret identities (which I actually really enjoy even though it frustrates me a bit). <br /><br /><b>
  <u>PLOT:</u>
</b> ★★☆☆☆<br /><b>
  <u>WRITING STYLE:</u>
</b> ★★★★☆<br /><b>
  <u>WORLD BUILDING:</u>
</b> ★★★☆☆<br /><b>
  <u>CHARACTERS:</u>
</b> ★★★☆☆<br /><b>
  <u>CHARACTER RELATIONSHIPS:</u>
</b> ★★★★★<br /><b>
  <u>THEMES:</u>
</b> ★★★★★<br /><b>
  <u>PACING:</u>
</b> ★★★☆☆<br /><b>
  <u>PAGE TURNER:</u>
</b> ★★★☆☆</span>
  <a data-text-id="17922586391885610802" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RcZ1M1pElExWBoj4RHpZt29SFkHS0uHMSEQErmt4pAMBZEs9WuNcnd0xJEUQAJQkSg2crqP4KcGSOa7PNvhewg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xH+9VsgotB5ZAt3Z0jJfwWEL0BUPE3+9VkGIGmboxdKA3YNYyI98z9I1cWSGSJJSRFRa+n45t7CMPCJ7O2g/Ew==')})
  }
